<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; top:941px;"><a name="2">Page 2</a></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:1034px; width:385px; height:14px;"><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:14px">Module Catalog: General Information and Notes to the Reader
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:1065px; width:475px; height:145px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">What is the module catalog?
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">One of the central components of the Bologna Process consists in the modularization of university
<br/>curricula, that is, the transition of universities away from earlier seminar/lecture systems to
<br/>a modular system in which thematically-related courses are bundled together into blocks, or
<br/>modules. 
<br/>This module catalog contains descriptions of all modules offered in the course of study.
<br/>Serving the goal of transparency in higher education, it provides students, potential students and
<br/>other internal and external parties with information on the content of individual modules, the goals
<br/>of academic qualification targeted in each module, as well as their qualitative and quantitative
<br/>requirements.
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:1226px; width:103px; height:11px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Notes to the reader:
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:1252px; width:470px; height:55px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Updated Information
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">An updated module catalog reflecting the current status of module contents and requirements is
<br/>published every semester. The date on which the module catalog was generated in TUMonline is
<br/>printed in the footer.
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:1322px; width:469px; height:100px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Non-binding Information
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">Module descriptions serve to increase transparency and improve student orientation with respect
<br/>to course offerings. They are not legally-binding. Individual modifications of described contents
<br/>may occur in praxis. 
<br/>Legally-binding information on all questions concerning the study program and examinations
<br/>can be found in the subject-specific academic and examination regulations (FPSO) of individual
<br/>programs, as well as in the general academic and examination regulations of TUM (APSO).

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:4811px; width:368px; height:9px;"><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:9px">Number of credits may vary according to degree program. Please see Transcript of Records.
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:4838px; width:479px; height:340px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Description of Examination Method:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">The examination consists of several exam courses (Prüfungsparcour). A semester-long project
<br/>work, which ends in the delivery of a business plan and in a presentation. The presentation
<br/>includes a prototype-demo of the developed product or service and a reflection on how innovative
<br/>entrepreneurs from the guest lectures lead high-tech organizations. Through the projectwork, it is
<br/>assessed how well the participants can identify and implement business opportunities. In teams
<br/>students recognize the needs and demands of the customers. Through customer feedback, field
<br/>interviews and contextual observations they synthesize the identified needs to translate them
<br/>into clear and significant customer benefits. Students develope business models to learn how to
<br/>bring the idea to the market and position the business with respect to competition. They learn the
<br/>systematic and iterativ approach of the Business Design for business model, team and technology
<br/>development.
<br/>Specifically with the examination deliverables, the participants demonstrate to what extent they
<br/>have developed the following competences:
<br/>- In their business plan participants formulate in a concise and structured way how they developed
<br/>an understanding about the actual customers and markets for their business idea.
<br/>- In their pitch presentation participants present their business idea before a jury of experts. The
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:10px">presentation includes a demo of the prototype for the developed product or service and a refelction
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">on how innovative entrepreneurs lead high-tech organizations.
<br/>Grading:
<br/>- 30% Prototype: As close to functional prototype as possible, must be interactive
<br/>- 30% Business plan read deck of 7 to 10 slides
<br/>- 40% 8-minute Pitch Presentation

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:5579px; width:478px; height:280px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Content:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">In a creative atmosphere, the participants learn to think through and present a business idea in the
<br/>structured form of
<br/>a business plan in order to solve a customer problem. For that purpose, fundamental chapters of a
<br/>business plan are
<br/>developed. Participants will network with people from the entrepreneurial environment of TUM, i.e.
<br/>as they connect with the guest lecturers.
<br/>The matter is developed in the following steps:
<br/>- The fundamentals of innovation
<br/>- Overview: Developing a business plan
<br/>- Consumer and consumer value
<br/>- Business model
<br/>- Assessment of business ideas
<br/>- Market &amp; competition
<br/>- Pitching business ideas
<br/>- Presentation practice: customer, customer value, market USP
<br/>- Forming powerful business teams
<br/>- Protection of intellectual property
<br/>- selected sessions from guest lecturers
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:5879px; width:476px; height:250px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Intended Learning Outcomes:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">At the end of the seminar the students will be able to:
<br/>- understand the difference between idea, invention, and innovation;
<br/>- understand the use of an iterative approach in the development of business opportunities;
<br/>- evaluate opportunities for business ideas and apply business concepts by prototyping, e.g. with
<br/>the help of a
<br/>business plan;
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:10px">- evaluate business ideas and identify business opportunities;
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">- segment markets and analyze potential niche markets;
<br/>- evaluate own business idea with the help of customer feedback, observations from stakeholders,
<br/>and interviews;
<br/>- identify a real customer problem and create customer benefit with ideas for a solution.
<br/>- understand effectual entrepreneurship;
<br/>- understand basic economic terms, such as Intellectual Property, Cashflow, Venture Capital,
<br/>Controlling;
<br/>- understand Design Thinking methodology;
<br/>Moreover through guest speakers’ lectures participants will be empowered to:

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:6381px; width:468px; height:40px;"><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">- realize opportunities and challenges associated with the founding and managing of technology-

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:6441px; width:475px; height:310px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Teaching and Learning Methods:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">The module is held in seminar-style: The lecturers are entrepreneurs, serial founders, coaches,
<br/>and former managing directors.
<br/>- Interdisciplinarity: Participants form cross-disciplinary teams to ensure a balanced mix of
<br/>expertise and skills in the
<br/>team.
<br/>- Action-based learning: All participants are encouraged to be proactive and to learn through
<br/>experience.
<br/>- Learning by doing: Each team develops a real business idea or one chosen for the seminar.
<br/>Particular attention is
<br/>paid to truly understanding the customer, for example, by interviews, observation, or expert
<br/>discussion.
<br/>- Prototyping: Using simple prototypes, the teams develop their business idea and make them
<br/>tangible.
<br/>- Online Networking: The work in the seminar is accompanied by online tools to support the team-
<br/>building and to generate ideas. The seminar is also accompanied by guest lectures of outstanding
<br/>founders, entrepreneurs, managers, or investors.  
<br/>- Elevator Pitch Training: Through the practice of elevator pitches, participants develop skills for
<br/>short and effective presentation of their business ideas.
<br/>- Presentation Training: Each team presents and defends their business idea twice before an
<br/>expert-jury and receives feedback on presentation style and content.

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:11081px; width:471px; height:130px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Description of Examination Method:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">The examination is a written and marked exam (120 minutes) in which only a non-programmable
<br/>calculator is allowed. The purpose of the exam is to verify the provided theoretical competences.
<br/>By exemplary business situation or compensation schemes, the students prove that they can
<br/>test and evaluate the suitability of certain instruments of value-based management. In concrete
<br/>cases, students are asked to apply the concept of residual income and potential accounting
<br/>adjustments, to calculate important key indicators of value-based management and to show
<br/>relationships between them and their effects in incentive schemes. The students are supposed to
<br/>realize occurring problems and to suggest solutions.
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:11231px; width:108px; height:25px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Repeat Examination:

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:11276px; width:364px; height:25px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">(Recommended) Prerequisites:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">Basic lectures in external accounting, Controlling, investment and financing
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:11321px; width:480px; height:160px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Content:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:10px">This module covers the different aspects of implementing value-based management in a company.
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">The focus of the course lies on the concept of residual income as corporate and business unit
<br/>performance measure: 
<br/>-Calculation of Economic Value Added (EVA) as the prevailing residual income measure in practice
<br/>including the most relevant accounting adjustments and their calculation.
<br/>- Introduction to the problems and proposed solutions of calculating the cost of capital.
<br/>- Discussion of the suitability of residual income as a goal congruent performance measure. 
<br/>- Design of compensation schedules to achieve the different and sometimes conflicting goals of
<br/>management compensation: alignment, wealth leverage, retention and minimizing shareholders’
<br/>cost of compensation.

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:11808px; width:477px; height:130px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Intended Learning Outcomes:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">The learning outcomes of this module are: (1) students will be able to remember and understand
<br/>the concept of residual income and value creation; (2) they will be able to analyze accounting
<br/>problems and problems related to incentives (compensation components and basis of
<br/>assessment);  (3) they will be able to apply the newly acquired knowledge to solve these problems
<br/>when designing and implementing value-based management for a company; (4) Therefore,
<br/>students evaluate different goals of management compensation and identify the suitability
<br/>of different tools such as employee stocks, stock options, the residual income with different
<br/>accounting adjustments as a performance measure or the application of a bonus bank.
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:11958px; width:479px; height:100px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Teaching and Learning Methods:

<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">delivered by presentations and discussions. In the exercise course the students apply the acquired
<br/>knowledge in solving exercises and implementing case studies. As a preparation of the exercise
<br/>courses, students solve exercises and the solutions are presented and discussed during the
<br/>exercise courses. Some exercises are solved in groups or individually and subsequently discussed
<br/>in the exercise course.

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:14649px; width:472px; height:100px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Description of Examination Method:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">The module examination is based on a written exam (90 minutes). By answering questions in text
<br/>form, students have to show their understanding of the concepts of discrete-time mathematical
<br/>modeling of financial markets and their capability to apply these concepts. They have to analyze
<br/>mathematical models of financial markets and solve given problems. Students have to determine
<br/>whether markets contain arbitrage, replicate and price given financial derivatives and develop
<br/>hedging strategies. The questions may include mathematical proofs and calculations.

<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">The module examination is based on a written exam (90 minutes). By answering questions in text
<br/>form, students have to show their understanding of the concepts of continuous-time mathematical

<br/>calculations and mathematical proofs, students have to demonstrate their ability to practically work
<br/>with the mathematical objects presented in the course and apply these mathematical objects to

<br/>methods for simulation, pricing and hedging. (If there are only few participants, an oral examination
<br/>might be held instead of a written exam).

<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">The module examination is based on an oral exam of at least 20 min per student. By answering
<br/>questions in oral form, students have to show their understanding of the core concepts of Digital
<br/>Innovation and Business Process Management as well as their knowledge of the scientific papers
<br/>discussed in the lecture. Moreover, students must be able to report on their own insights from
<br/>applying software tools in the tutorials. The oral examination will typically be for groups of three
<br/>students at the same time in order for the students to show their ability to use technical terms
<br/>correctly in an academic discussion.

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:18943px; width:480px; height:130px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Teaching and Learning Methods:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">The module consists of a lecture with integrated tutorials. The topics of the lecture are presented
<br/>via slides. In order to have the students deal in more depths with the topics, these are critically
<br/>discussed in the group on a regular basis. At the same time, selected scientific papers are
<br/>discussed together with the students. The scientific papers must be prepared by the students
<br/>for such discussions according to predefined questions. Within the tutorials, the solutions to
<br/>exercise sheets are developed in close cooperation with the lecturers. The exercise sheets contain
<br/>mathematical exercises and case studies. Furthermore, software tools, e.g., for process mining are
<br/>introduced by the lecturers and applied by the students in the context of the case studies.

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:20000px; width:471px; height:175px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Description of Examination Method:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">The module examination is based on a 90 minutes written exam. The written exam may be
<br/>replaced by an oral examination, however, if the number of participants is low. By answering
<br/>questions in written form, students show their understanding of the role of information systems
<br/>for today's and future’s energy system, and hence, of exemplary concepts and approaches in
<br/>the areas of smart markets, smart grid, smart factory, smart mobility, and smart home. By doing
<br/>calculations, students demonstrate their ability to work with and apply the mathematical methods
<br/>presented during the lectures and the tutorials. They must also discuss the presented concepts
<br/>and approaches. Students can bring a non-programmable and non-finance calculator, and two
<br/>self-prepared (hand- or machine-written) double-sided DIN-A4 sheets with notes (i.e., in total four
<br/>pages with notes). Papers discussed in class can be brought to the exam as long as they do not
<br/>contain any notes (highlights are allowed).
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:20195px; width:108px; height:25px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Repeat Examination:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">Next semester
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:20240px; width:162px; height:11px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">(Recommended) Prerequisites:
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:20285px; width:473px; height:115px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Content:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">In the first part of the module, students learn about physical and technical basics of energy
<br/>supply, energy transmission, and energy demand. Moreover, the module addresses the basics
<br/>of sustainable electricity markets and relevant sectors, e.g., mobility. In the second part of the
<br/>module, students learn and discuss how digital technologies can help overcome challenges of
<br/>modern energy systems, for example, the highly relevant topics of a low-carbon energy transition
<br/>or lowering CO2 emissions. The lecture presents insights from various energy-related areas, e.g.,
<br/>smart markets, smart grid, smart factory, smart mobility, and smart home.

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; top:20563px;"><a name="24">Page 24</a></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:20593px; width:276px; height:9px;"><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:9px">WIBT0002: Digital Energy Management | Digital Energy Management
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:20651px; width:480px; height:145px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Intended Learning Outcomes:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">Students understand the key challenges of low-carbon energy transitions. Moreover, they know
<br/>potential solutions that digital technologies and information systems can offer for these challenges.
<br/>Based on this knowledge, students can evaluate and classify basic techno-economic issues in the
<br/>context of energy management. Besides lecture-style teaching, we use interactive elements such
<br/>as discussions of current digital trends, joint analysis of scientific papers, and exercises. Students
<br/>thus not only acquire theoretical knowledge but also gain practically relevant qualifications.
<br/>The lecture prepares students for jobs in strategic IT management, energy management,
<br/>consulting, research or business model development, energy-start-ups, utilities, and energy-related
<br/>companies.
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:20816px; width:474px; height:145px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Teaching and Learning Methods:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">The course consists of lectures and complementary, interactive tutorials. Exercises are available
<br/>online before each tutorial, and we develop solutions collaboratively with the students during the
<br/>tutorials. However, students should prepare for the exercises in advance to identify questions and
<br/>to allow for detailed discussions of the identified issues. In the lectures, we discuss topics from a
<br/>scientific and often quantitative perspective. Students should thus have a basic understanding of
<br/>mathematical and statistical models. They should also be willing to follow mathematical reasoning
<br/>and comprehend quantitative research papers. Moreover, we present different approaches and
<br/>methods to assess various real-world problems and show how scientific results can inform real-
<br/>world decision-makers.

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:21801px; width:471px; height:190px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Description of Examination Method:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">The module's examination consists of a group presentation and a term paper. Concerning the
<br/>group presentation, the students have to present their findings, followed by a discussion. The
<br/>presentation has to be didactically well-structured and must focus on the students' core findings.
<br/>The students moderate their discussion and must answer questions by the audience (i.e., the
<br/>lecturers, advisors, and other seminar groups). Students must also actively participate in the
<br/>discussions moderated by other seminar groups. The assessment considers both the group-wise
<br/>and the individual performance of the examinees. Thereby, the students have to demonstrate
<br/>their ability to collaborate in a goal-oriented manner, create structured presentations, and present
<br/>the content of these presentations in oral form. By writing the term paper, students have to show
<br/>their understanding of the research problem and their ability to develop and discuss innovative
<br/>solutions. They have to demonstrate their academic writing skills and their ability to present
<br/>academically advanced ideas clearly and concisely.

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:22570px; width:468px; height:115px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Teaching and Learning Methods:

<br/>the advisor. To do so, the students read related work, create own ideas, and prepare these ideas
<br/>for the presentation with the advisor. The advisor provides the students repeated feedback and
<br/>provides guidance on the directions in which the students’ ideas should be further developed.
<br/>Approaching an academic and/or practical question in teams and developing an own approach
<br/>enables students to evaluate existing approaches and analyze strengths and weaknesses to
<br/>create own academic ideas in an interdisciplinary team.

<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">Examination is based on a final project and its presenation. In the final project and presentation,

<br/>classmates will be given the opportunity to ask questions.
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:29054px; width:108px; height:25px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Repeat Examination:

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:29144px; width:460px; height:145px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Content:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">The course focuses around three pillars:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:10px">i) Individuals: how do we make saving and investing decisions? What biases can cloud our
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">decisions?
<br/>ii) Managers: do managers exhibit similar biases? How do managers behave if markets are not
<br/>efficient?
<br/>iii) Financial Markets: are markets fully efficient? Are stock returns predictable?
<br/>In addition to the key behavioral finance concepts, students will develop and reinforce a set of
<br/>analytical tools related to corporate finance and investment decisions. We'll also consider how
<br/>behavioral principles can help develop new financial services and products for consumers

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:32508px; width:368px; height:9px;"><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:9px">Number of credits may vary according to degree program. Please see Transcript of Records.
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:32534px; width:478px; height:235px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Description of Examination Method:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">The examination consists of the elaboration of a business plan and a presentation of it. Based
<br/>on the business plan, the following requirements are checked: if students can design, test and
<br/>implement a business idea based on criteria like access to the market, customer desirability,
<br/>prototyping, distribution, calculation and financing. In the business plan, all aspects of a new
<br/>business model are partially described. Students particularly show what value proposition they can
<br/>offer to defined customer groups. They estimate the market potential and analyze the competition.
<br/>They study feasible marketing strategies, test them on the market and present the results.
<br/>Based on those they develop distribution strategies to reach relevant target groups. Additionally
<br/>considering the results of their field tests, interviews and prototypes, the students create scenarios
<br/>for business models. They identify and evaluate estimations for the financial planning based on
<br/>tested and validated business hypotheses (customer, market, costs, returns …). Finally the results
<br/>are delivered by the team in a business idea presentation. During the presentation students are
<br/>asked critical questions by the examiners. Thereby it can be checked, if students are able to
<br/>distribute tasks in a team according to competences and experiences, and therefore to test and
<br/>validate dozens of hypotheses and to create a business plan in a structured way.

<br/>- evaluate own business idea with the use of customer feedback, observations of stakeholders and
<br/>interviews,
<br/>- plan a business concept in order to apply for the, e.g. EXIST-funding or to participate in business
<br/>plan competitions, 
<br/>- assess whether certain business idea represents a real business opportunity.

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:36140px; width:108px; height:25px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Repeat Examination:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">End of Semester
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:36185px; width:452px; height:40px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">(Recommended) Prerequisites:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">MA0009 Introduction to Probability and Statistics (or former modules: MA1401 Introduction to
<br/>Probability Theory, MA2402 Basic Statistics)
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:36245px; width:471px; height:145px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Content:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">This course introduces the principles of actuarial science with a focus on non-life insurance.
<br/>We cover pricing methods, capital allocation, the individual model and the collective model. The
<br/>relevant stochastic models for tariff calculation, loss reserving and reinsurance are developed
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:10px">and discussed. Different loss-reserving methods are introduced and compared. As non-life
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">insurance (automotive, liability, fire, etc.) is heavily influenced by the random nature of claim
<br/>arrivals (frequency) and sizes (severity), stochastic tool such as credibility theory, stochastic
<br/>processes, extreme-value analysis and dependence modelling are introduced in the present
<br/>context. The role of reinsurance in risk-sharing is analyzed from a mathematical perspective. The
<br/>current regulation (Solvency II) is briefly discussed.
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:36410px; width:478px; height:40px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Intended Learning Outcomes:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">After successful completion of the module, the students are able to understand and apply the main
<br/>stochastic methods in the practice of (non-life) insurance.

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:37838px; width:477px; height:130px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Description of Examination Method:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">The module examination is based on a written exam (90 minutes) with theoretical and practical
<br/>components. Students have to show their theoretical understanding of a generalized linear
<br/>regression model by answering questions on model set-up and assumptions, the generalized least
<br/>squares estimation methodology, finite and asymptotic properties as well as hypothesis testing.
<br/>In the practical section, students have to demonstrate their understanding of the methodology
<br/>on an economically motivated application. By analyzing and interpreting results from a variety of
<br/>candidate models, students are led to reach a decision about the most plausible model for the
<br/>application at hand.  
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:37988px; width:108px; height:11px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Repeat Examination:
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:38033px; width:162px; height:25px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">(Recommended) Prerequisites:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">none
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:38078px; width:475px; height:85px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Content:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:10px">This course is an intensive introduction to various econometric concepts like sampling, estimation,
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">hypotheses testing, and (generalized) linear regression used in applied financial research. The
<br/>emphasis will be on developing and applying regression-based techniques in both cross-sectional
<br/>and time-series contexts. Their usefulness will also be examined in the light of current financial
<br/>studies.
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:38183px; width:481px; height:70px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Intended Learning Outcomes:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">After successful completion of the module, students are able to analyze cross-sectional and time-
<br/>series data with regression-based techniques. Furthermore, students can develop and calibrate
<br/>econometric models that can be used to test theories or to make forecasts. They understand the
<br/>properties and limitations of these models and are able to assess how they fit different applications.

<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">The certificate of achievement is accomplished by the presentation of the own case solution
<br/>(verbal, 40%), the discussion of another group’s case solution (verbal, 10%), and the written

<br/>solution. In the discussion, students must challenge the case solution of another group. In the
<br/>written report, students have to apply finance theory to practical issues. Hereby, a crucial point is to
<br/>address the feedback of the presentation and discussion.

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:41417px; width:481px; height:145px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Description of Examination Method:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">The grading is based on an open-book e-test with a duration of 90 minutes. The e-test consists
<br/>of calculations and multiple choice questions. By answering questions in multiple choice or text
<br/>form, students have to show that they are able to understand the theory behind Asset Management
<br/>(e.g. concept of utility and the calculation of basic utility measures, portfolio selection under various
<br/>constraints, determinants of the capital asset pricing model and other factor models).
<br/>Moreover they show their ability to explain the basic models e.g. of portfolio theory.
<br/>By performing calculations and elaborating on theoretical considerations, students demonstrate
<br/>their ability to evaluate and apply the methods presented in the module. They show that they are
<br/>able to consider asset pricing models.

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:42056px; width:452px; height:85px;"><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">- Theory and application of basic models of portfolio theory with a particular focus on portfolio
<br/>optimization under various contraints in the Markowitz mean-variance framework
<br/>- Theory and application of asset pricing models (e.g. Capital Asset Pricing Model, Arbitrage
<br/>Pricing Theory)
<br/>- Theory and application of conditional asset pricing
<br/>- Portfolios Performance Measurement
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:42162px; width:481px; height:160px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Intended Learning Outcomes:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">After successful completion of the module, students (1) understand the concept of utility theory
<br/>(utility functions and link to risk attitudes) and can (2) calculate basic utility measures (absolute risk
<br/>aversion, relative risk aversion, expected utility, certainty equivalent, risk premium); Students can
<br/>also (3) explain and apply the basic models of portfolio theory, i.e. they can calculate the optimal
<br/>portfolio allocation in the Markowitz mean-variance framework for an arbitrary set of asset returns
<br/>under various constraints. Moreover, students (4) understand the fundamental concept of the
<br/>Capital Asset Pricing Model and are able to (5) apply the model and its variants introduced in the
<br/>module and also recognize the shortcomings of this model. Students (6) learn to use other asset
<br/>pricing models and when to apply them. Finally, students (7) learn the theory, process and methods
<br/>to measure the portfolios’ performance.
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:42342px; width:446px; height:130px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Teaching and Learning Methods:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">The module combines various learning methods:
<br/>- Basic knowledge, theoretical concepts and practical examples will be provided through the
<br/>lecture.
<br/>- Controversial discussions and active participation in class are encouraged to deepen
<br/>understanding of the concepts presented.
<br/>- In the exercises, students will apply their theoretical knowledge to concrete
<br/>- Demonstration of how to apply portfolio optimization on real-world data by using Excel
<br/>- Students will get insights into practice via several guest lecture

<br/>and equity financing and that they know how to apply, value and analyse the respective financing
<br/>instruments.

<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">The module deals with the opportunities and limitations of financing from the perspective of

<br/>introduced and discussed. Their functions within an optimal financial strategy in the company are
<br/>outlined. After understanding the basics of financing and the systematic of financial statements
<br/>as well as financial forecasting, these elements are put into practice by setting up an integrated

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:46516px; width:478px; height:85px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Intended Learning Outcomes:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">Students will learn the major fundamentals of econometrics. The course focuses on linear
<br/>regression models and maximum likelihood methods for cross sectional and panel data. Moreover,
<br/>the course covers methods for limited dependent variables. By studying these topics students will
<br/>learn how to chose an appropriate method of analysis on the basis of the research question and
<br/>the data. The ultimate goal is then to apply these methods.

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:47710px; width:471px; height:190px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Description of Examination Method:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">The module's examination consists of a group presentation and a term paper. Concerning the
<br/>group presentation, the students have to present their findings, followed by a discussion. The
<br/>presentation has to be didactically well-structured and must focus on the students' core findings.
<br/>The students moderate their discussion and must answer questions by the audience (i.e., the
<br/>lecturers, advisors, and other seminar groups). Students must also actively participate in the
<br/>discussions moderated by other seminar groups. The assessment considers both the group-wise
<br/>and the individual performance of the examinees. Thereby, the students have to demonstrate
<br/>their ability to collaborate in a goal-oriented manner, create structured presentations, and present
<br/>the content of these presentations in oral form. By writing the term paper, students have to show
<br/>their understanding of the research problem and their ability to develop and discuss innovative
<br/>solutions. They have to demonstrate their academic writing skills and their ability to present
<br/>academically advanced ideas clearly and concisely.

<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">The module examination is based on a presentation of the own case solution and a written report
<br/>by each group (2-4 students). In the presentation, the focus lies on the structure and content
<br/>of the presented case solution. In the written report, students must show their understanding of
<br/>emerging technologies in the field of business and information systems engineering by applying
<br/>their knowledge of emerging technologies to a real-world use case.

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:51445px; width:476px; height:115px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Content:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">The first part of the module teaches the students digital technologies by introducing nine related
<br/>technology groups, especially IoT, AI, and Blockchain. The second part deals with technology
<br/>application to real-world examples from the economy and energy sector to teach socio-technical
<br/>and entrepreneurial implications of emerging technologies. The module familiarizes students with
<br/>the essential concepts of digital technologies such as artificial intelligence, blockchain, the Internet
<br/>of things, process mining as well as related applications in diverse domains, e.g., in the fields of
<br/>energy informatics, digital innovation, business process management, and digital value networks.

<br/>entrepreneurial impact of emerging digital technologies on the business and energy sector.
<br/>Furthermore, they are familiar with the concepts of emerging digital technologies, especially IoT,

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:51928px; width:479px; height:100px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Teaching and Learning Methods:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">The module consists of two parts. The first part is lecture and a corresponding exercise. In the
<br/>lecture the relevant emerging digital technologies are conveyed. Students also read literature

<br/>to assess various real-world problems are presented to show how scientific results can inform real-
<br/>world applications. In the second part, students then apply their knowledge to real-world scenarios
<br/>to solve problem sets and case studies.

<br/>documentation of maximum three pages (40%) covering idea development, team development and
<br/>used tools.

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:54933px; width:197px; height:11px;"><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">Final Deliverable 1: Functional Prototype
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:54963px; width:471px; height:71px;"><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">- Functional prototype in hard- and/or software
<br/>- Not a final product, but should showcase at least one key aspect of your product/service
<br/>- For software, use any framework, IDE, language etc. that works
<br/>- For hardware, use MakerSpace &amp; prototype budget (up to 250€ per team, only redeemable with
<br/>invoice!)
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:55053px; width:170px; height:11px;"><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">Final Deliverable 2a: Final Demo…
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:55083px; width:455px; height:71px;"><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">- You will have exactly 7 minutes, incl. your video of up to 2 minutes; and Q&amp;A thereafter
<br/>- Your demo (incl. video) should include: Team, Customer Need, Value Proposition, Prototype,
<br/>Competition, Differentiation, Future Roadmap (Note: content is same as the read deck)
<br/>- All team members must present
<br/>- Slides should not distract from the presenter (e.g. too much text, low contrast, …)

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:55795px; width:458px; height:55px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">(Recommended) Prerequisites:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">Knowledge: Willingness to participate; affinity with tech and entrepreneurship trends preferred

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:55870px; width:475px; height:220px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Content:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">- Kick-off: Introduction to challenges, resources, objectives. “Challenge fair” at the end. Students
<br/>are sensitized, inspired and stimulated to develop feasible, viable and holistic solutions to address
<br/>current industrial topics as smart city, mobility, digital healthcare, Industry 4.0 and smart grid by
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:10px">utilizing cutting-edge technologies as cloud, IoT, AI, AR/VR.
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">- Challenge workshops: 1 day is reserved for each corporate to hold an interactive workshop with
<br/>the batch of students interested to know more about the respective challenge (known needs,
<br/>available technologies, boundary conditions, etc.).
<br/>- Interdisciplinary teams and ideas registration as pertaining to a specific challenge (choice made
<br/>by teams): Team, Vision, Project Plan
<br/>- Ideation workshop: Design thinking, empathic exploration, needfinding, concept generation,
<br/>evaluation, and selection
<br/>- Work-in-progress: Prototyping, testing, generating feedback, iterating, creating new insights and
<br/>elaborating use cases. On demand office hours and consulting sessions with experts for ideation,
<br/>technology development, product design, and team development.

<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:56462px; width:317px; height:25px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Intended Learning Outcomes:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">Upon successful completion of this module, students are able to: 
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:56506px; width:480px; height:251px;"><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">- identify latest technology trends related to topics such as smart city, mobility, digital healthcare,
<br/>Industry 4.0 and smart grid  
<br/>- understand opportunities and challenges in applying cutting-edge technology (e.g., cloud, IoT, AI,
<br/>AR/VR) to address a specific industrial challenge
<br/>- conduct project-based interdisciplinary teamwork 
<br/>- carry out an individualized learning process by utilizing referenced online resources as well as
<br/>on demand expert coaching regarding team development, technology development and product
<br/>design
<br/>- evaluate own ideas, prototypes and project findings with experts, users, and customers, and work
<br/>closely with their feedback
<br/>- recognize and utilize contemporary web platforms for digital project creation and sharing
<br/>- operate in a high-tech prototyping workshop equipped with latest technology and devices
<br/>- create functional prototypes to demonstrate own proposed solution to a specific industrial
<br/>challenge
<br/>- devise a showcase of own project results to a broad audience of peers, academics and
<br/>practitioners
<br/>- create short business plans to effectively communicate business value of own project results
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:56776px; width:463px; height:41px;"><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">Thus, students get familiarized with the many facets of entrepreneurship. In doing that, they are
<br/>enabled to see, realize, and experience the multiplicity in the everyday life of an entrepreneur,
<br/>entrepreneurial personalities, as well as entrepreneurial skills and motivations. 
<br/></span></div>, <div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:56px; top:56837px; width:466px; height:70px;"><span style="font-family: Arial-BoldMT; font-size:11px">Teaching and Learning Methods:
<br/></span><span style="font-family: ArialMT; font-size:11px">Innovatively addressing complex themes as smart city and Industry 4.0 often requires the use of
<br/>cutting-edge technologies within an entrepreneurial process. Based on this premise and to get
<br/>the students understand and apply such a process, the module deploys hands-on project-based
<br/>learning and interdisciplinary teamwork.

<br/>corporates, who provide access to their proprietary technologies, resources, experts and coaches
<br/>specific to their respective challenge. An industrial challenge is formulated to be broad, with the
